- Term 1: `3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 0.05899*367.02 + 1)` = `3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 22.65)` = `-0.2139*epsilon*T + 82.09*epsilon`

So GT = `c_a*T*epsilon + c_b*epsilon + c_c*epsilon^c_d*exp(c_e/T) + c_f*epsilon*exp(-(T-c_g)^2)`

The key features are:
1. A `T*epsilon` term (linear in both T and epsilon)
2. An `epsilon` term
3. An `epsilon^0.4475 * exp(const/T)` term - fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius-like term
4. An `epsilon * exp(-(T-const)^2)` term - Gaussian in T

The Gaussian term `exp(-(T-367)^2)` is extremely distinctive. For T values away from 367, this term is essentially zero (it's a very narrow Gaussian). None of the candidates contain `exp(-(T-...)^2)` or any squared T terms in exponents.

Let me check if the Gaussian term might be negligible. The coefficient is 5.1243, and `exp(-(T-367)^2)` is only non-negligible when T ≈ 367. For |T - 367| > ~3, this term is essentially 0 (exp(-9) ≈ 0.0001). So this term creates a sharp spike near T=367.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
```
3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*(T - 367.02) + 1) + 94.205*epsilon^0.4475*exp(-55.016/(8.314*T)) + epsilon*5.1243*exp(-(T - 367.02)^2)
```

Let me expand the first term:
```
3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 0.05899*367.02 + 1)
= 3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 21.65 + 1)
= 3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 22.65)
= -0.2139*epsilon*T + 82.10*epsilon
```

So GT = **A*epsilon*T + B*epsilon + C*epsilon^0.4475*exp(D/T) + E*epsilon*exp(-(T-F)^2)**

where A, B, C, D, E, F are specific constants.

Key structural features of GT:
1. Term linear in epsilon*T
2. Term linear in epsilon
3. Term with epsilon^(~0.45) * exp(const/T) — fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type T dependence
4. Term with epsilon * exp(-(T-const)^2) — Gaussian in T multiplied by epsilon

The T-dependence is critical: we have linear T, exp(const/T), and exp(-(T-const)^2). These are three fundamentally different functions of T.
